free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_films&amp;redirect=no" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox <span style="font-size:85%;">(<i>1</i>\xe2\x80\x93<i>5</i>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Country</th><td>\nUnited States</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Language</th><td>\nEnglish</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Budget</th><td>\n<span style="font-size:85%;"><b>Total (5 films):</b></span><br />$1.274&#160;billion</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Box office</th><td>\n<span style="font-size:85%;"><b>Total (5 films):</b></span><br />$4,524,358,182</td></tr></tbody></table> \n<p><i><b>Pirates of the Caribbean</b></i> is a series of <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">fantasy</a> <a href="/wiki/Swashbuckler_film" title="Swashbuckler film">swashbuckler films</a> produced by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Bruckheimer" title="Jerry Bruckheimer">Jerry Bruckheimer</a> and based on <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walt Disney</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(attraction)" title="Pirates of the Caribbean (attraction)">theme park ride of the same name</a>.\n</p><p>Directors of the series include <a href="/wiki/Gore_Verbinski" title="Gore Verbinski">Gore Verbinski</a> (<i>1</i>\xe2\x80\x93<i>3</i>), <a href="/wiki/Rob_Marshall" title="Rob Marshall">Rob Marshall</a>&#160;(<i>4</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Joachim_R%C3%B8nning" title="Joachim R\xc3\xb8nning">Joachim R\xc3\xb8nning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Espen_Sandberg" title="Espen Sandberg">Espen Sandberg</a> (<i>5</i>). The series is primarily written by <a href="/wiki/Ted_Elliott_(screenwriter)" title="Ted Elliott (screenwriter)">Ted Elliott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terry_Rossio" title="Terry Rossio">Terry Rossio</a> (<i>1</i>\xe2\x80\x93<i>4</i>); other writers include <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Beattie" title="Stuart Beattie">Stuart Beattie</a> (<i>1</i>), <a href="/wiki/Jay_Wolpert" title="Jay Wolpert">Jay Wolpert</a> (<i>1</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Nathanson" title="Jeff Nathanson">Jeff Nathanson</a> (<i>5</i>). The stories follow the adventures of <a href="/wiki/Jack_Sparrow" title="Jack Sparrow">Captain Jack Sparrow</a> (<a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>), <a href="/wiki/Will_Turner" title="Will Turner">Will Turner</a> (<a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">Orlando Bloom</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Swann" title="Elizabeth Swann">Elizabeth Swann</a> (<a href="/wiki/Keira_Knightley" title="Keira Knightley">Keira Knightley</a>). Characters such as <a href="/wiki/Hector_Barbossa" title="Hector Barbossa">Hector Barbossa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Rush" title="Geoffrey Rush">Geoffrey Rush</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Joshamee_Gibbs" title="Joshamee Gibbs">Joshamee Gibbs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kevin_McNally" title="Kevin McNally">Kevin McNally</a>) follow Jack, Will and Elizabeth in the course of the films. The fourth film features <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Blackbeard" title="List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters">Blackbeard</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ian_McShane" title="Ian McShane">Ian McShane</a>) and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Angelica" title="List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters">Angelica</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz" title="Pen\xc3\xa9lope Cruz">Pen\xc3\xa9lope Cruz</a>), while the fifth film features <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Armando_Salazar" title="List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters">Armando Salazar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Javier_Bardem" title="Javier Bardem">Javier Bardem</a>), <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Henry_Turner" title="List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters">Henry Turner</a> (<a href="/wiki/Brenton_Thwaites" title="Brenton Thwaites">Brenton Thwaites</a>) and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Carina_Barbossa" title="List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters">Carina Smyth</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kaya_Scodelario" title="Kaya Scodelario">Kaya Scodelario</a>). The films take place in a fictionalized historical setting; a world ruled by the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, the East India Trading Company (based on the real <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, with pirates representing freedom from the ruling powers.\n</p><p>The film series started in 2003 with <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl">Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl</a></i>, which received positive reviews from critics and grossed <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>654 million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-List_By_Box_Office_Sales_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-List_By_Box_Office_Sales-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> After the first film\'s success, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> revealed that a trilogy was in the works. The franchise\'s second film, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest">Dead Man\'s Chest</a></i>, was released three years later in 2006; the sequel proved successful, breaking financial records worldwide the day of its premiere. <i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i> ended up being the number one film of the year upon earning almost $1.1 billion at the worldwide box office. The third film in the series, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End">At World\'s End</a></i>, followed in 2007 earning $960 million, and Disney released a fourth film, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides">On Stranger Tides</a></i>, in 2011 in conventional 2D, <a href="/wiki/Digital_3-D" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital 3-D">Digital 3-D</a> and <a href="/wiki/IMAX_3D" class="mw-redirect" title="IMAX 3D">IMAX 3D</a>. <i>On Stranger Tides</i> succeeded in also grossing more than $1 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-List_By_Box_Office_Sales_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-List_By_Box_Office_Sales-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> becoming the second film in the franchise and only the eighth film in history to achieve this.\n</p><p>The franchise has grossed over $4.5 billion worldwide;<sup id="cite_ref-List_By_Box_Office_Sales_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-List_By_Box_Office_Sales-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_franchises_and_film_series" class="mw-redirect" title="List of highest-grossing franchises and film series">twelfth-highest-grossing film series</a> of all time and it was the first franchise where more than one film grossed $1 billion worldwide.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" (2003)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Dead_Man&#39;s_Chest_(2006)"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i> (2006)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#At_World&#39;s_End_(2007)"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext"><i>At World\'s End</i> (2007)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#On_Stranger_Tides_(2011)"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext"><i>On Stranger Tides</i> Bloom and Knightley did not return for the fourth film and had cameo appearances for the fifth film.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span id="The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl_.282003.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl_(2003)"><i>The Curse of the Black Pearl </i> (2003)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The Curse of the Black Pearl (2003)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl">Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl</a></div>\n<p>Blacksmith <a href="/wiki/Will_Turner" title="Will Turner">Will Turner</a> teams up with eccentric pirate <a href="/wiki/Jack_Sparrow" title="Jack Sparrow">Captain Jack Sparrow</a> to save Turner\'s love, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Swann" title="Elizabeth Swann">Elizabeth Swann</a>, from cursed pirates led by Jack\'s mutinous former first mate, <a href="/wiki/Captain_Barbossa" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain Barbossa">Captain Barbossa</a>. Jack wants revenge against Barbossa, who left him stranded on an island before stealing his ship, the <i>Black Pearl</i>, along with 882 pieces of cursed Aztec Gold.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Dead_Man.27s_Chest_.282006.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dead_Man\'s_Chest_(2006)"><i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i> (2006)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Dead Man&#039;s Chest (2006)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man\'s Chest</a></div>\n<p>Lord <a href="/wiki/Cutler_Beckett" title="Cutler Beckett">Cutler Beckett</a> of the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Trading Company</a> arrests Will and Elizabeth for aiding Captain Jack Sparrow in the previous film. Beckett offers <a href="/wiki/Clemency" class="mw-redirect" title="Clemency">clemency</a> if Will agrees to search for Jack\'s compass in a bid to find the <a href="/wiki/Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Dead Man&#39;s Chest">Dead Man\'s Chest</a>\xe2\x80\x94and inside, the heart of villainous <a href="/wiki/Davy_Jones_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)" title="Davy Jones (Pirates of the Caribbean)">Davy Jones</a>\xe2\x80\x94which would give Beckett control of the seas. However, Jack wants the Chest to escape from an unpaid debt with Jones, who made Jack captain of the <i>Black Pearl</i> for 13 years in exchange for 100 years of service aboard Jones\' ship, the <i>Flying Dutchman</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="At_World.27s_End_.282007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="At_World\'s_End_(2007)"><i>At World\'s End</i> (2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: At World&#039;s End (2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End">Pirates of the Caribbean: At World\'s End</a></div>\n<p>Lord Beckett gains power over Davy Jones and, with the help of the <i>Flying Dutchman</i>, he is now executing his plans to extinguish piracy forever. To stand against the East India Trading Co., Will, Elizabeth, Barbossa, and the crew of the <i>Black Pearl</i> set out to rescue Captain Jack Sparrow from <a href="/wiki/Davy_Jones%27_Locker" title="Davy Jones&#39; Locker">Davy Jones\' Locker</a>. As one of the Nine Pirate Lords, Jack is needed in order to release an ancient goddess with the power to defeat Beckett\'s forces.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="On_Stranger_Tides_.282011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="On_Stranger_Tides_(2011)"><i>On Stranger Tides</i> (2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: On Stranger Tides (2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides">Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides</a></div>\n<p>Captain Jack Sparrow is on a quest to find the fabled <a href="/wiki/Fountain_of_Youth" title="Fountain of Youth">Fountain of Youth</a> and crosses paths with a former lover, Angelica. She forces Jack aboard the <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne%27s_Revenge" title="Queen Anne&#39;s Revenge">Queen Anne\'s Revenge</a></i>, a ship captained by the infamous pirate <a href="/wiki/Blackbeard" title="Blackbeard">Blackbeard</a>, Angelica\'s father. Both are also in search of the Fountain; Angelica to save her father\'s soul, Blackbeard to escape a prophecy of his demise at the hands of a one-legged man. Joining the hunt is former pirate captain Barbossa, now a privateer in <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">King George II</a>\'s Navy, who is in a race against the Spanish for the Fountain of Youth.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Dead_Men_Tell_No_Tales_.282017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dead_Men_Tell_No_Tales_(2017)"><i>Dead Men Tell No Tales</i> (2017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Dead Men Tell No Tales (2017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Men_Tell_No_Tales" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Men Tell No Tales">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Men Tell No Tales</a></div>\n<p>Ghost Spanish Royal Navy soldiers led by Jack Sparrow\'s old nemesis, Captain Armando Salazar, escape from the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Triangle" title="Bermuda Triangle">Devil\'s Triangle</a>, with the goal of killing every pirate at sea, including him. To survive, Jack seeks out the legendary <a href="/wiki/Trident_of_Poseidon" title="Trident of Poseidon">Trident of Poseidon</a>, a powerful artifact whose owner can control the seas and break curses.<sup id="cite_ref-THR_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Upcoming:_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_6_.28TBA.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Upcoming:_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_6_(TBA)">Upcoming: <i>Pirates of the Caribbean 6</i> (TBA)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Upcoming: Pirates of the Caribbean 6 (TBA)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shortly before the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides">On Stranger Tides</a></i>, it was reported that Disney was planning to shoot the fifth and the sixth films back-to-back,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> although it was later revealed that only the fifth film was in development. On March 4, 2017, director <a href="/wiki/Joachim_R%C3%B8nning" title="Joachim R\xc3\xb8nning">Joachim R\xc3\xb8nning</a> stated that <i>Dead Men Tell No Tales</i> was only the beginning of the final adventure, implying that it would not be the last film of the franchise and that a sixth film could be released.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2017, producer Jerry Bruckheimer indicated that another <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> sequel is still possible if <i>Dead Men Tell No Tales</i> does well in its home release.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\nIn October 2017, <a href="/wiki/Kaya_Scodelario" title="Kaya Scodelario">Kaya Scodelario</a> said that she was contracted to return for a sixth film.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Joachim_R%C3%B8nning" title="Joachim R\xc3\xb8nning">Joachim R\xc3\xb8nning</a> is being eyed to direct the film.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The film is still in development, as of August 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Short_film">Short film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Short film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Tales_of_the_Code:_Wedlocked_.282011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tales_of_the_Code:_Wedlocked_(2011)"><i>Tales of the Code: Wedlocked</i> (2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tales of the Code: Wedlocked (2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Wenches Scarlett (Lauren Maher) and Giselle (<a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Branch" title="Vanessa Branch">Vanessa Branch</a>) fix each other up for their wedding, in which they would each marry their groom. Upon realizing that both their grooms were the same man\xe2\x80\x94Jack Sparrow\xe2\x80\x94the two wenches find themselves in an auction led by the Auctioneer. The short film serves as a prequel to <i>The Curse of the Black Pearl</i>, explaining just why Jack Sparrow\'s boat, <i>the Jolly Mon</i>, was seen sinking at the beginning of the whole story, and explaining why wenches Scarlett and Giselle were so upset with him, and it also implies how Cotton lost his tongue. The plot took inspiration from the "Auction scene" from the original ride.\n</p><p>The short was directed by <a href="/wiki/James_Ward_Byrkit" title="James Ward Byrkit">James Ward Byrkit</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wedlocked_on_Jim_Byrkit&#39;s_official_website_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wedlocked_on_Jim_Byrkit&#39;s_official_website-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and was only included as a special feature in the US 15-disc 3D Blu-ray/2D Blu-ray/DVD + Digital Copy box set that includes films 1\xe2\x80\x934; and in the similar UK five-disc set.\n</p><p>Byrkit conceived the idea for the project while on sets Rick Heinrichs designed for <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man\'s Chest</a></i> (2006) and <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End">Pirates of the Caribbean: At World\'s End</a></i> (2007). As the pirate cove sets from the feature films\xe2\x80\x94where the short film takes place\xe2\x80\x94were set to be demolished, the short project was prepped in a matter of days and shot over three days. Byrkit based the short film on the Pirate Code Book as it was a device that could tie into other stories later.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_film">First film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: First film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the early 1990s<sup id="cite_ref-Perfection_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perfection-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> screenwriters <a href="/wiki/Ted_Elliott_(screenwriter)" title="Ted Elliott (screenwriter)">Ted Elliott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terry_Rossio" title="Terry Rossio">Terry Rossio</a> conceived a <a href="/wiki/Supernatural" title="Supernatural">supernatural</a> spin on the pirate genre after completing work on <i><a href="/wiki/Aladdin_(1992_Disney_film)" title="Aladdin (1992 Disney film)">Aladdin</a></i>, but there was no interest from any studio. Undeterred, the writing team refused to give up the dream, waiting for a studio to pick up their take on a pirate tale.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Disney had <a href="/wiki/Jay_Wolpert" title="Jay Wolpert">Jay Wolpert</a> write a script based on the <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(attraction)" title="Pirates of the Caribbean (attraction)">Pirates of the Caribbean</a></i>, which producer <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Bruckheimer" title="Jerry Bruckheimer">Jerry Bruckheimer</a> rejected, feeling it was "a straight pirate movie".<sup id="cite_ref-Talk_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talk-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Bruckheimer brought <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Beattie" title="Stuart Beattie">Stuart Beattie</a> in to rewrite the script in March 2002, due to his knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Greg_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greg-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and later that month Elliott and Rossio were brought in.<sup id="cite_ref-Talk_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talk-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Elliott and Rossio, inspired by the opening narration of the <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> ride, decided to give the film a supernatural edge.<sup id="cite_ref-Writers_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Writers-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> As the budget rose, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Eisner" title="Michael Eisner">Michael Eisner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Iger" title="Bob Iger">Robert Iger</a> threatened to cancel the film, though Bruckheimer changed their minds when he showed them concept art and <a href="/wiki/Animatics" class="mw-redirect" title="Animatics">animatics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2002 <a href="/wiki/Gore_Verbinski" title="Gore Verbinski">Gore Verbinski</a> signed on to direct <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl">The Curse of the Black Pearl</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Rush" title="Geoffrey Rush">Geoffrey Rush</a> signed on the following month to star.<sup id="cite_ref-Greg_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greg-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Verbinski was attracted to the idea of using modern technology to resurrect a genre, one that had disappeared after the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Hollywood" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Hollywood">Golden Age of Hollywood</a>, and recalled his childhood memories of the ride, feeling the film was an opportunity to pay tribute to the "scary and funny" tone of it. Depp was attracted to the story as he found it quirky: rather than trying to find treasure, the crew of the <i>Black Pearl</i> were trying to return it in order to lift their curse; also, the traditional mutiny had already taken place. Verbinski approached Rush for the role of Barbossa, as he knew he would not play it with attempts at complexity, but with a simple villainy that would suit the story\'s tone.<sup id="cite_ref-Director_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Director-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">Orlando Bloom</a> read the script after Rush, with whom he was working on <i><a href="/wiki/Ned_Kelly_(2003_film)" title="Ned Kelly (2003 film)">Ned Kelly</a></i>, suggested it to him.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Keira_Knightley" title="Keira Knightley">Keira Knightley</a> came as a surprise to Verbinski: he had not seen her performance in <i><a href="/wiki/Bend_It_Like_Beckham" title="Bend It Like Beckham">Bend It Like Beckham</a></i> and was impressed by her audition.<sup id="cite_ref-Director_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Director-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Wilkinson" title="Tom Wilkinson">Tom Wilkinson</a> was negotiated with to play Governor Swann,<sup id="cite_ref-Greg_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greg-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> but the role went to <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Pryce" title="Jonathan Pryce">Jonathan Pryce</a>, whom Depp idolized.<sup id="cite_ref-Director_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Director-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shooting for <i>The Curse of the Black Pearl</i> began on October 9, 2002 and wrapped by March 7, 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Greg_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greg-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Before its release, many executives and journalists had expected the film to flop, as the pirate genre had not been successful for years, the film was based on a theme-park ride, and Depp rarely made a big film.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> However, <i>The Curse of the Black Pearl</i> became both a critical and commercial success.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_and_third_films">Second and third films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Second and third films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After seeing how well the first film was made, the cast and crew signed for two sequels to be shot back-to-back,<sup id="cite_ref-pirates02_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pirates02-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> a practical decision on Disney\'s part to allow more time with the same cast and crew.<sup id="cite_ref-Plan_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plan-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Writers Ted Elliott and Terry Rossio knew that with an ensemble cast, they weren\'t free to invent totally different situations and characters, as with the <i><a href="/wiki/Indiana_Jones_(franchise)" title="Indiana Jones (franchise)">Indiana Jones</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">James Bond</a></i> series, and so had to retroactively turn <i>The Curse of the Black Pearl</i> into the first of a trilogy.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> They wanted to explore the reality of what would happen after <a href="/wiki/Will_Turner" title="Will Turner">Will Turner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Swann" title="Elizabeth Swann">Elizabeth Swann</a>\'s embrace at the end of the first film, and initially considered the <a href="/wiki/Fountain_of_Youth" title="Fountain of Youth">Fountain of Youth</a> as the plot device.<sup id="cite_ref-Chart_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chart-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> They settled on introducing <a href="/wiki/Davy_Jones_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)" title="Davy Jones (Pirates of the Caribbean)">Davy Jones</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Flying_Dutchman_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)" title="Flying Dutchman (Pirates of the Caribbean)">Flying Dutchman</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Kraken_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)" title="Kraken (Pirates of the Caribbean)">Kraken</a>, a mythology mentioned twice in the first film. They introduced the historical <a href="/wiki/East_India_Trading_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="East India Trading Company">East India Trading Company</a> (also mentioned in the first film), which for them represented a counterpoint to the themes of personal freedom represented by pirates.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Filming for the sequels began on February 28, 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-VoyageBegins_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VoyageBegins-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> with <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest">Dead Man\'s Chest</a></i> finishing on March 1, 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End">At World\'s End</a></i> on January 10, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Aloha_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aloha-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The second film was also the first Disney theatrical feature film with the computer-generated <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> logo.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fourth_film">Fourth film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Fourth film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Rossio and Elliot discovered the novel <i><a href="/wiki/On_Stranger_Tides" title="On Stranger Tides">On Stranger Tides</a></i> during production of <i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i> and <i>At World\'s End</i> and decided to use it as the basis for a fourth film. As Gore Verbinski was unavailable, Bruckheimer invited <a href="/wiki/Rob_Marshall" title="Rob Marshall">Rob Marshall</a> to direct the film.<sup id="cite_ref-Collider_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collider-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Elliott and Rossio decided to do a stand-alone film,<sup id="cite_ref-Making_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Making-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> with a story that would support new characters,<sup id="cite_ref-Making2_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Making2-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and incorporate elements from the novel, such as <a href="/wiki/Blackbeard" title="Blackbeard">Blackbeard</a>, the Fountain of Youth and mermaids\xe2\x80\x94the latter two having been already alluded to in the previous films.<sup id="cite_ref-Rossio_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rossio-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Depp, Rush, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Ellis_(actor)" title="Greg Ellis (actor)">Greg Ellis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_McNally" title="Kevin McNally">Kevin McNally</a> returned to their roles,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and the cast saw the additions of <a href="/wiki/Ian_McShane" title="Ian McShane">Ian McShane</a> as Blackbeard and <a href="/wiki/Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz" title="Pen\xc3\xa9lope Cruz">Pen\xc3\xa9lope Cruz</a> as Angelica, Blackbeard\'s daughter and Jack Sparrow\'s love interest.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> A further addition was <a href="/wiki/Richard_Griffiths" title="Richard Griffiths">Richard Griffiths</a> as King <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George II of Great Britain</a>. After the costly production of two simultaneous films, Disney tried to scale down the fourth installment, giving a lower budget,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> which led to cheaper locations and fewer scenes with special effects.<sup id="cite_ref-Budget_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Budget-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> It was also filmed in <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a>, with cameras similar to the ones used in <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collider_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collider-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Filming for <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides">On Stranger Tides</a></i> began June 14, 2010 and ended on November 19, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Budget_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Budget-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> It was released in the United States on May 20, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> With a budget of $378.5 million, <i>On Stranger Tides</i> holds the record for <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_films" title="List of most expensive films">most expensive film ever made</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fifth_film">Fifth film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Fifth film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On January 14, 2011, it was confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Terry_Rossio" title="Terry Rossio">Terry Rossio</a> would write the screenplay for the fifth installment, without his co-writer <a href="/wiki/Ted_Elliott_(screenwriter)" title="Ted Elliott (screenwriter)">Ted Elliott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On January 11, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Nathanson" title="Jeff Nathanson">Jeff Nathanson</a> signed on to write the script for the film. On May 29, 2013, it was announced that Norwegian directors <a href="/wiki/Joachim_R%C3%B8nning" title="Joachim R\xc3\xb8nning">Joachim R\xc3\xb8nning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Espen_Sandberg" title="Espen Sandberg">Espen Sandberg</a> were selected to direct.<sup id="cite_ref-Pirates_5_directors_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pirates_5_directors-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On August 22, 2013, the two revealed that the title of the fifth film would be <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Men_Tell_No_Tales" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Men Tell No Tales">Dead Men Tell No Tales</a></i>, alluding to the line well-known from the <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> theme park attractions.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Although, the film was given an alternative title, <i>Salazar\'s Revenge</i>, in selected European, South American and Asian countries for marketing purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> They also confirmed that they were working on the film, speaking highly of Jeff Nathanson\'s "funny and touching" script and that they are inspired by the first film, <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl">The Curse of the Black Pearl</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On September 10, 2013, Disney pushed back the film\'s initial 2015 release,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> with sources indicating that a Summer 2016 release is likely.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Producer Jerry Bruckheimer revealed that script issues were behind the delay, and that Jeff Nathanson was at work on a second attempt based on a well-received outline.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> While Disney originally announced a release on July 7, 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-blogs.disney.com_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.disney.com-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dead Men Tell No Tales</i> was released on May 26, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline_Hollywood_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline_Hollywood-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A spokesman for the Australian Arts Minister confirmed that the fifth installment was set to shoot in Australia after the government agreed to repurpose $20 million of <a href="/wiki/Tax_incentive" title="Tax incentive">tax incentives</a> originally intended for the remake of <i>20,000 Leagues Under the Sea</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> According to Australian film industry sources, pre-production started in late September 2014 with filming expected to commence in February 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Mail_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Mail-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> This was officially confirmed by Disney and <a href="/wiki/Ian_Walker_(politician)" title="Ian Walker (politician)">Ian Walker</a> the <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> Arts Minister on October 2, 2014, stating that filming will take place exclusively in Australia, being the largest production to ever shoot in the country. <a href="/wiki/Village_Roadshow_Studios" title="Village Roadshow Studios">Village Roadshow Studios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_Douglas,_Queensland" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Douglas, Queensland">Port Douglas</a> were officially confirmed as filming locations.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Production began in Australia on February 17, 2015 and wrapped on July 9, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Recurring_cast_.26_characters"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Recurring_cast_&amp;_characters">Recurring cast &amp; characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Recurring cast &amp; characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters" title="List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters">List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters</a></div>\n<blockquote class="toccolours" style="text-align:justify; width:100%; float:center; padding: 5px 5px 5px 5px; display:table;">\n<b><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">List indicator(s)</div></b>\n<ul><li>This table shows the recurring characters and the actors who have portrayed them throughout the franchise.</li>\n<li>A dark grey cell indicates the character was not in the film, or that the character\'s presence in the film has not yet been announced.</li>\n<li>A <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cameo"><sup>C</sup></span>  indicates a <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo appearance</a>.</li>\n<li>A <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_likeness"><sup>L</sup></span>  indicates an appearance wherein an actor\'s facial features were digitally imprinted upon another actor\'s face.</li>\n<li>A <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_young"><sup>Y</sup></span>  indicates an appearance as a younger version of a pre-existing character.</li></ul>\n</blockquote>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="3" style="width:15%;">Character\n</th>\n<th the Black Pearl">The Curse of the Black Pearl</a></i>\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center; width:15%;"><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest">Dead Man\'s Chest</a></i>\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center; width:15%;"><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End">At World\'s End</a></i>\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center; width:15%;"><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tales">Dead Men Tell No Tales</a></i>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>2003\n</th>\n<th>2006\n</th>\n<th>2007\n</th>\n<th>2011\n</th>\n<th>2017\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Jack_Sparrow" title="Jack Sparrow">Jack Sparrow</a>\n</th>\n<td colspan="4"><a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a><sup id="cite_ref-Director_17-3" class="reference"><a Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office_performance">Box office performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Box office performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: center" width="99%">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2">Film\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">U.S. release class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM5-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;">Total\n</th>\n<th>$<span class="nowrap"><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7009145178083300000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>1,451,780,833</span>\n</th>\n<th>$<span class="nowrap"><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7009307257734900000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>3,072,577,349</span>\n</th>\n<th>$<span class="nowrap"><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7009452435818200000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>4,524,358,182</span>\n</th>\n<th>14\n</th>\n<th>10\n</th>\n<th>$1.452 billion\n</th>\n<th><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>The <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> film series was successful at the box office, with each film grossing over $650&#160;million, and all but <i>Dead Men Tell No Tales</i> at some point ranking among the fifty <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">highest-grossing films of all time</a>. It also became the first ever series to have multiple films passing the billion dollar mark in box office revenues with <i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i> and <i>On Stranger Tides</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> since <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films#Highest-grossing_franchises_and_film_series" title="List of highest-grossing films">followed by other film franchises</a>.\n</p><p><i>The Curse of the Black Pearl</i> was the third-highest-grossing 2003 film in North America (behind <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i>) and fourth worldwide (behind <i>The Return of the King</i>, <i>Finding Nemo</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Matrix_Reloaded" title="The Matrix Reloaded">The Matrix Reloaded</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i> was the most successful film of 2006 worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> and <i>At World\'s End</i> led the worldwide grosses in 2007, though being only fourth in North America (behind <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_3" title="Spider-Man 3">Spider-Man 3</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_the_Third" title="Shrek the Third">Shrek the Third</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> <i>On Stranger Tides</i> was the third-highest-grossing film of 2011 worldwide (behind <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows \xe2\x80\x93 Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows \xe2\x80\x93 Part 2</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Transformers:_Dark_of_the_Moon" title="Transformers: Dark of the Moon">Transformers: Dark of the Moon</a></i>) and the fifth in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The first three sequels broke box office records upon release, of which the most notable are the opening-weekend record in North America (<i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> the Memorial-Day weekend record in North America (<i>At World\'s End</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and the opening-weekend record outside North America (<i>On Stranger Tides</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_and_public_response">Critical and public response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Critical and public response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:99%; text-align:center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Film\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl">The Curse of the Black Pearl</a></i>\n</td>\n<td>79% (210 reviews)<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>63 (40 reviews)<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>A<sup id="cite_ref-POTCcs_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTCcs-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest">Dead Man\'s Chest</a></i>\n</td>\n<td>54% (220 reviews)<sup id="cite_ref-RT2_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT2-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>53 (37 reviews)<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>A\xe2\x88\x92<sup id="cite_ref-POTCcs_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTCcs-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End">At class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>A\xe2\x88\x92<sup id="cite_ref-POTCcs_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTCcs-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides">On Stranger Tides</a></i>\n</td>\n<td>32% (262 reviews)<sup id="cite_ref-RT4_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT4-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>45 (39 reviews)<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>B+<sup id="cite_ref-POTCcs_109-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTCcs-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Men_Tell_No_Tales" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Men Tell No Tales">Dead Men Tell No Tales</a></i>\n</td>\n<td>30% (230 reviews)<sup id="cite_ref-RT5_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT5-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>39 (45 reviews)<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>A\xe2\x88\x92<sup id="cite_ref-POTCcs_109-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTCcs-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The series is noted for its high quality of acting talent, and is one of the aspects of the films that is always praised.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-richardroeper.com_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richardroeper.com-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Variety_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The visual and practical effects are considered some of the best ever done on film,<sup id="cite_ref-richardroeper.com_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richardroeper.com-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Variety_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> so much so that audiences believed certain <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CGI</a> elements of the films were real and done practically.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oscars2004_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oscars2004-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> However, the plots of the four sequels have received mixed reviews, with the general consensus that they are too bloated and convoluted to follow.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> is noted for reinvigorating the pirate genre of film after decades of either no pirate films or failed pirate films.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The success of the series saw Disney and Jerry Bruckheimer try to replicate the franchise\'s success by launching films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Persia:_The_Sands_of_Time_(film)" title="Prince of Persia: The Sands of Time (film)">Prince of Persia: The Sands of Time</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lone_Ranger_(2013_film)" title="The Lone Ranger (2013 film)">The Lone Ranger</a></i>, the latter of which directed by Gore Verbinski. Both movies failed critically and commercially.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_the_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_franchise" class="mw-redirect" title="List of accolades received by the Pirates of the Caribbean franchise">List of accolades received by the Pirates of the Caribbean franchise</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Academy_Awards">Academy Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Academy Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Together, all the first three films were nominated for a total of 11 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a>, of which a single award was won.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:left;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="width:214px;" rowspan="2">Award\n</th>\n<th colspan="5">Film\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><i>The Curse of the Black Pearl</i>\n</th>\n<th><i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i>\n</th>\n<th><i>At World\'s End</i>\n</th>\n<th><i>On Stranger Tides</i>\n</th>\n<th><i>Dead Men Tell No Tales</i>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Actor">Actor in a Leading
